              <span id="reviewTextContainer196698835" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer187833738526847473">8/26/2012. <br/>What did I just read? This doesn't even make sense. I was hoping I could leave off this series on a good note, to cleanly wipe it from my memory so I wouldn't constantly be thinking about what a piece of crap the last few books were. But no. James Patterson couldn't even do that.<br/><br/>Lets start with Fangs story. It begins with him and his gang getting attacked by...wait for it...Ari! <br/>*Going back to when the rough draft of Nevermore was being written*<br/><br/>JP: Hey how many times have we brought A</span>
  <span id="freeText187833738526847473" style="display:none">8/26/2012. <br />What did I just read? This doesn't even make sense. I was hoping I could leave off this series on a good note, to cleanly wipe it from my memory so I wouldn't constantly be thinking about what a piece of crap the last few books were. But no. James Patterson couldn't even do that.<br /><br />Lets start with Fangs story. It begins with him and his gang getting attacked by...wait for it...Ari! <br />*Going back to when the rough draft of Nevermore was being written*<br /><br />JP: Hey how many times have we brought Ari back to life?<br /><br />Ghost Writer #1: Uh....four?<br /><br />JP: I think that's got another use left in it, don't you think? It worked pretty well in the first book.<br /><br />Ghost Writer #2: As long as we get paid.<br /><br />*James Patterson thinking about what he should have happen next*<br /><br />JP:Why don't we kill off Maya?<br /><br />Ghost Writer #1: Don't you think that might be a little too convenient?<br /><br />JP: No way. No one's gonna see this one coming. I mean, it gives a direct route for Fang to go back to Max without feeling like he has abandoned his gang. Plus, now Maya won't be in the way of <i>Fax</i>.<br /><br />Ghost Writer #1: Fax?<br /><br />JP: It's what all the kids are calling it these days.<br /><br />*Later*<br /><br />JP: Let's think of something romantic for Dylan to do...<br /><br />Ghost Writer #2: Oooh I got it! Let's have Dylan make a tiny tree house so he can seduce Max in it with food and candles.<br /><br />Ghost Writer #3: But make sure Gazzy films it. Our fans want sex tapes!<br /><br />*Gets to the part where Fang shows up*<br /><br />JP: Okay, now let's make sure Max isn't angry or confused even though she just made out with Dylan.<br /><br />Ghost Writer #1: This can be the part where Dylan realizes that he has to kill Fang.<br /><br />Ghost Writer #2: And this can be the part where Fang doesn't care that the person he has been having eye sex with all month just died.<br /><br />JP: Sounds Perfect. *Get's up from chair.* I'm gonna go get a coffee. You kids keep going. *Walks out the door*<br /><br />Ghost Writer #1: I don't remember what happened in any of the previous books. Do you guys?<br /><br />*Shakes heads*<br /><br />Ghost Writer #1:...Oh well. Okay, now let's have Dylan <i>attack</i> Fang so that Max will hate him.<br /><br />Ghost Writer #3: Then let's make an island paradise where Max and Fang can make out in a hammock....in a tree...<br /><br />Ghost Writer #2: And then the world should end with-<br /><br />Ghost Writer #3: A massive wave-<br /><br />Ghost Writer #2: I was going to say disease but okay.<br /><br />*Checks watch*<br /><br />Ghost Writer #1: Guys, how is Max going to save the world? We only have twenty minutes left before Doctor Who comes on.<br /><br />Ghost Writer #2: Not to worry. James left us a note saying that Max doesn't need to save the world. She just has to tell Fang she loves him.<br /><br />Ghost Writer #3: Great. I got it. All the mutants are getting evacuated into a cave by Angel and her flock. But Max's hormones take control and she stays with Fang. Angel tells her she's the voice. Max basically ignores this and continues to undress Fang with her eyes. She, Fang, Dylan, and Angel survive the wave.<br /><br />Ghost Writer #1: And then Max goes to check on the others.<br /><br />Ghost writer #3: No, let's do one of those cool cliff-hanger things like they did in Catching Fire and Inception. Where they don't know if they died or not.<br /><br />Ghost Writer #1: But it's the last book in the series!<br /><br />Ghost Writer #2: No one cares about Iggy, Gazzy, and Nudge anyway.<br /><br />Ghost Writer #1: So what do we do?<br /><br />Ghost Writer #3: Fax.<br /><br /><br /><br />Thank you James Patterson for getting me into reading. I am truly grateful. And thank you for teaching me not to get my hopes up about sequels. *Starts crying* Thank you for curing me of my ridiculous obsession with love. (I congragulate you if you get that reference). And thank-you Cassandra Clare for creating Will Herondale so I'm not one of those girls that go "FAXXX TRULUV4EVA!" <br /><br />And most of all, Mr. Patterson, thank you for ruining one of my favorite series. I will not be picking up confessions of a murder suspect. or any other book by you for that matter. I owe you nothing.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="187833738526847473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Tilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9886489-tilly"><img alt="Tilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599658929p2/9886489.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/382427485?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tilly" href="/user/show/9886489-tilly">Tilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9886489-tilly?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9886489-tilly?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer382427485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16915721931884849641"><i>The end isn't near, it's here</i><br/><br/>2.5 stars.<br/><br/>Where do I begin? <i>I was very excited for this book and had high hopes for it, keep that in mind.</i><br/><br/>First off, NEVERMORE was always going to be well written. It's <i>James Patterson</i> for goodness sake. That dude could make the back of a cereal box captivating.<br/><br/>But I'm certain I'm not the only one who feels that NEVERMORE, was a bit of a let down in other aspects.<br/>It started by Max almost swooning over Dylan, with hardly a mention of Fang or even 'her baby' Angel, who</span>
  <span id="freeText16915721931884849641" style="display:none"><i>The end isn't near, it's here</i><br /><br />2.5 stars.<br /><br />Where do I begin? <i>I was very excited for this book and had high hopes for it, keep that in mind.</i><br /><br />First off, NEVERMORE was always going to be well written. It's <i>James Patterson</i> for goodness sake. That dude could make the back of a cereal box captivating.<br /><br />But I'm certain I'm not the only one who feels that NEVERMORE, was a bit of a let down in other aspects.<br />It started by Max almost swooning over Dylan, with hardly a mention of Fang or even 'her baby' Angel, who had previously been bird-kidnapped. It was purely Max getting drawn into those 'aquamarine' eyes, with almost no worry about Angel. She didn't even properly mourn her until a little later in the book. (Granted, she did have a cry later. With Dylan.) <br /><br />Then it cuts to Fang's gang, where we have some secondary characters that could have been amazing, but we didn't really hear much about them sadly, just like in Angel. That was a shame. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ But, then who returns, again? A certain wolfy-kid who just happens to be Max's half bro. Yeah that's right, Ari-Jesus is back, for a third time. Honestly, couldn't we have had a better villain? I'm tired of Ari.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Then some more stuff happens <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(Clone death, treason, blah) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> . And Angel's point of view is added to the chapters. <br /><br />I honestly have no qualms with the Angel chapters. They were haunting, damn scary and I want a whole book of them. <br /><br />Back to Max. More stuff happens that is pretty much irrelevant, like a candlelit dinner in a tree house, with her PERFECT blue eyed beau. I think that's my problem with Dylan. Or should I say my other problem. My first problem is that he came between Max and Fang. My second problem is that he's perfect and it's boring. He's a one dimensional character in my opinion. Every secondary character in the book pretty much adores him, and even Max is pulled in for a part of it. I don't know if Mr Patterson wanted to make us love Dylan or hate him, but for me, it was the latter. <br /><br />Cut to Angel. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The whitecoats have experimented on her like Iggy and she's lost her sight. I did not see that coming, that bit was good. Jeb and Max's mom turn out to be traitors; haven't we been here before? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Back to Fang. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A voice in his head tells him to be with Max. So he goes to her. He falls off a cliff beforehand. (I am really glad Fang and Max ended up together though!)<br /><br />Dylan becomes majorly pissed and he sulks upstairs. Until the next day when Max and Fang realise they love each other so he goes off and Dylan Hulk-smashes the town. <br /><br />More stuff happens, they find Angel, hear more about the doomsday group, yawn. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />This plot, over the course of MAX to NEVERMORE I think, has been the most tedious. In THE ANGEL EXPERIMENT it was literally; we're bird kids and we kick ass and discover we have powers. Then it turned into, global warming is bad. (I preferred the first books)<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Once they're all home, Ari -I mean Jesus Wolf- knocks on the door. Apparently Fang has something in his DNA to help science with finding about Immortality. Yes. So he must die! <br /><br />Fang, obviously refuses to get a noose for him, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> so the Flock all kick butt like old times! Except it didn't really feel the same, I don't think I even read the familiar old words 'Roundhouse kick'. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ari dies again (But no doubt, he'll have survived the apocalypse somehow. Kidding.) then Max's mom turns up in a copter. She makes a really unconvincing argument about how she had her mind controlled by Jeb. Max asks Angel if she's being truthful, and Angel says she is. <br /><br />Blah blah, they go to a place called Paradise, minus Dylan, things are looking good for the Flock, but then Dylan somehow finds them on an island in the middle of nowhere, and announces that the apocalypse is coming. The kids get into the caves, except Max, Fang, Angel and Dylan. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There were a few pages that kept me hooked after that, about how you should live every day like it's your last and I enjoyed that.<br /><br />Then, it was 'the end'. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The world was pretty much gone, apart from a world of trees, ocean and stuff. Angel, Max, Fang and Dylan survived, and they were saying how this world was meant for them, and it was the time of the Bird Kids.<br /><br />None of the remaining Flock even questioned whether Nudge, Gazzy and Iggy had possibly survived in the cage, or fussed over how they were going to find them. That was my main rage point.<br />The book was left on an ending where we had no idea what happened to three of the flock. Granted, they weren't the main members, but I really wanted to know exactly what happened.<br /><br />For example; did Angel ever fully regain her sight? Was Max reunited with Iggy and co? Angel was the voice in Max's head, was she the voice in the other flock members'? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I don't mind unanswered questions with a short series, or just a stand alone novel, but COME ON. It's Maximum Ride, it's such a long series. ALL I WANT ARE ANSWERS.<br /><br />To be honest, I wish that there had been <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the death of a flock member <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Then I would have felt more emotion towards this book.<br /><br />We had to wait a year and a half for this. <br /><br />Now, this review is kind of angry, so sorry if you had to read it and you're now angry too, it's just I had to vent my rage somewhere.<br />I've tried to combine this with good things, like the Angel chapters and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Max/Fang getting back together <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but there just aren't many good things in my opinion.<br /><br />I'm devastated Maximum Ride, a series that I've been hooked on forever, has ended, especially with an ending like this.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16915721931884849641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/276582571" />
    <a title="Peanut Butter Jelly Time" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7576309-peanut-butter-jelly-time"><img alt="Peanut Butter Jelly Time" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365387765p2/7576309.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/276582571?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peanut Butter Jelly Time" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peanut Butter Jelly Time" href="/user/show/7576309-peanut-butter-jelly-time">Peanut Butter Jelly Time</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">All Max Fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7576309-peanut-butter-jelly-time?shelf=read-again-and-again">read-again-and-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7576309-peanut-butter-jelly-time?shelf=bad-boys">bad-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7576309-peanut-butter-jelly-time?shelf=profound-insights">profound-insights</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7576309-peanut-butter-jelly-time?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer276582571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14109238273065515024"><b> BEFORE READING NEVERMORE: </b><br/><br/>Dear James Patterson:<br/><br/>First of all, I really, really hope you wrote/are writing this book yourself. Not with a bunch of crap ghost writers who don't know Max and her gang and clearly never read the books, since they made Max all damsel-y and the flock all whiney. It seems after the first three you got tired of the Flock.<br/>RIGHT THERE YOU KNOW WHEN TO STOP A SERIES.<br/>But really, you wanted to milk it, didn't you? You sicko, you knew we'd never be able to resist not knowing w</span>
  <span id="freeText14109238273065515024" style="display:none"><b> BEFORE READING NEVERMORE: </b><br><br>Dear James Patterson:<br><br>First of all, I really, really hope you wrote/are writing this book yourself. Not with a bunch of crap ghost writers who don't know Max and her gang and clearly never read the books, since they made Max all damsel-y and the flock all whiney. It seems after the first three you got tired of the Flock.<br>RIGHT THERE YOU KNOW WHEN TO STOP A SERIES.<br>But really, you wanted to milk it, didn't you? You sicko, you knew we'd never be able to resist not knowing what happened to Max and the flock next!<br><br>I hope you tie up all these loose ends. Because really, when you think about it, you could have ended the series with STWAOES if you'd just <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ gotten Max to accept Fang. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Everything was tied up at that point. But no, you just had to open it up again for your pathetic excuse for a fourth novel!<br><br>I'm glad you've decided to end the series. This is wonderful growth. I'm sure you made a lot of $$$ off the last couple of plotless MR books, and I really hope that Nevermore is AWESOME. End this baby with a bang!<br><br>But I do appreciate that you brought MR to the world in the first place. What would we do without the flock? For that, I thank you.<br>Thank you.<br>Thank you.<br>Also, I like the cover.<br><br>Sincerely,<br>A Rabid Fan<br><br>P.S. Oh, and JP? Make it good. No pressure or anything.<br><br><br><b> EDIT- POST-NEVERMORE </b><br>My first thought after reading the last page of the epilogue of this book<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380369683i/722448._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="WHOA" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>WHEN exactly did Maximum Ride become so... intense? Thought-provoking? Deep?? JP must have hired a different ghostwriter for this book. It was really unsettling. And the ending? WTF was up with that? I had no idea what was going on there.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380369683i/722449.jpg" width="350" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Granted, I was very very glad when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Fang and Max got together. However, I did NOT appreciate how Fang was first like, "OMG Maya let's make a fresh start together!" and then when Maya died (I hate when love triangles are resolved by someone dying) he turned around to Max, and, both disregarding the reasons they had split in the first place, proceeded to make out in a "honeymoon" suite (although, that bit was VERY swoony). I thought the coming back together should be a little slower, a little more realistic. But since Max is a SUCKER, she jumped right back into Fang's delicious arms and.... *swoon* But ANYWAY, disregarding the fact that I may or may not have also done that (I'm not feminist material, I guess :P), I wish it was a little more like their love in the first 3 books; slowly falling for each other-again.<br><br>But then Dylan went INSANE and started attacking Fang, and I was like JAYSUS CROYST SUPERSTAR . But you know, Fang just rolled with it, even though he didn't know why the hell Dyl was attacking him, like a boss. <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380369683i/722450._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="750" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> But supposedly Fang isn't as strong as Dylan. Which I strongly do not agree with.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>FANG as usual was SWOON-WORTHY. *sigh*<br><br>So, final thoughts? This book was much better than the last couple. But not at the level of the first three books. Worth your money, a sort-of mind-blowing but not quite satisfying ending, and for me a bittersweet ending. I discovered Max and the flock almost three years ago, and I've read the series over and over since. I'm sad to see them go. But all good things must end. <br><br>And so ends the story of Maximum Ride.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

  <span id="freeText13615740720263556638" style="display:none">This review was written when I was thirteen, so if it seems a little...immature, that's why! I'm going to leave it as it is, though. It sums up the raw anger coursing through my soul when I had finished reading this book. ;)<br /><br />-----<br /><br />I CAN'T FREAKING WAIT!!!!!!! FAX! FAX FAX FAX!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! Seriously. I think I'm dying. I just finished rereading Angel and I....argh!!! THIS SERIES HAS THE WORST LOVE TRIANGLE OF ALL TIME!!! <br /><br />WHAT???!?!?!?! IT'S NOW COMING OUT IN AUGUST?!?!!?!? GOODREADS AND THE END OF ANGEL <b>BOTH</b> SAID IT WAS FEBRUARY!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! SCREAAAAMMMMMMMMMM!!!!!!!!!!!!! NOOO!!!!<br /><br />Oh, there's a cover now? Meh. This one's just a bit....silvery. I mean, for the hair. Hopefully she did not experience so much stress as to turn her hair grey. (I assume that's Max on the cover.)<br /><br />I. HATE. YOU. JAMES. PATTERSON. OR WHOEVER IS RESPONSIBLE FOR THIS HORRIFIC CHANGE OF EVENTS, THUS SHATTERING LIFE AS I KNOW IT FOREVER.<br /><br />Reread Fang....not a good idea...<br /><br />So, the first book had about 100,000 ratings. This one has not even half that. Sad.<br /><br />*UPDATE: READ*<br /><br />I really wish I could have loved it. I do. I really, honestly do. <br /><br />But I didn't. <br /><br />The more I think about it, which I don't particularly want to do (that is why I've delayed writing a review), the more I realize how much Nevermore disappointed me. True, one of the biggest (if not THE biggest), most agonizing love triangles I've ever read was resolved--and Max ended up with the right boy. But how it happened was not at all satisfactory. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maya dies, so Fang decides to go back to Max, and, voila--he suddenly knows that he loves her?? And she just abandons Dylan to be with Fang?! Not that I really like Dylan, still--but that's harsh. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And the ending. Just, what the heck?! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The whole series was about how Max was going to save the world. She was MADE to save the world, or so we were told. And then a meteorite, or whatever it is, crashes into the earth and kaboom, most of the population is dead and Max is all, "Oh, la dee da. Most of the population is dead, but <i>we're</i> fine, <i>we</i> have gills and wings." What about all the other people you met? What about the poor schmucks who lived on the rest of the earth? What about the kids you met at the various schools you've been to? You heartless....$#@. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There were too many things left unresolved from the earlier books. For example, what happened to Anne, from the second book? Was Sam really an Eraser, or not? What happened to him? Total, who was one of my favorite characters, was sort of abandoned. The romance took up a lot more of the book than was really necessary. One good point, though, is that Fang was no longer described as "dark" every other sentence. I was about ready to tear my hair out about that. And the rest of the flock was also abandoned, more or less. Iggy never gets any funny lines anymore. Gazzy hardly ever makes use of his "talent," nor does he blow stuff up. Nudge is totally self-absorbed, no longer the sweet little girl she used to be. And she goes out on a date with a sixteen year old. That's so gross. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She also wanted to get her wings hacked off, in this very book, and James Patterson did not deal with that, either. Apparently the end of the world is enough to make you forget to resolve any petty details you may have left hanging. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> At least Iggy and Ella got together, which was sort of cute. I wish they'd mentioned Ella's dog Magnolia, though.<br /><br />There were many other silly, unnecessary things in this book which made me want to scream. I was so excited about this book. I was in agony about the love triangle. And then James Patterson took my excitement, anticipation, and hopes that Nevermore would redeem the crap that was the last two books, jumped on it with cleats, ran it through a shredder, stuffed the mutilated remains into a garbage bag, and threw it off the Empire State Building. That's how disappointed I was.<br /><br />I'm still attached enough to Max and the rest of the flock (and still in love with Fang, I guess--the old Fang) to give this two stars. I'm just not willing to accept that it's over and not as phenomenal as I expected and wanted. <br /><br />(But by the way, I DID learn a new word. "Clowder." In the words of Max, "look it up. You'll learn something.") </span>
  <a data-text-id="13615740720263556638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_334824760" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/334824760" />
    <a title="Carrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7531367-carrie"><img alt="Carrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513207591p2/7531367.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/334824760?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie" href="/user/show/7531367-carrie">Carrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7531367-carrie?shelf=read-in-middle-school">read-in-middle-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer334824760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8162005834958200365">This is going to be a very hard review. On one hand, the book in general fell somewhere between <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1829709.The_Final_Warning__Maximum_Ride___4_' title='The Final Warning (Maximum Ride, #4) by James Patterson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Final Warning</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7201913.Angel__Maximum_Ride___7_' title='Angel (Maximum Ride, #7) by James Patterson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angel</a>. On the other hand, I can't really bring myself to give it a bad review. <br/><br/>Ok. So first of all, it wasn't that bad if you set goals. Mine were <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ 1) FAX!!!!!!!!! and 2) no one important dies. Luckily, both of these happened.  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Unfortunately, just because those two expectations were met doesn't mean the book actually made complete sense. It was a bi</span>
  <span id="freeText8162005834958200365" style="display:none">This is going to be a very hard review. On one hand, the book in general fell somewhere between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1829709.The_Final_Warning__Maximum_Ride___4_" title="The Final Warning (Maximum Ride, #4) by James Patterson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Final Warning</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7201913.Angel__Maximum_Ride___7_" title="Angel (Maximum Ride, #7) by James Patterson" rel="nofollow noopener">Angel</a>. On the other hand, I can't really bring myself to give it a bad review. <br /><br />Ok. So first of all, it wasn't that bad if you set goals. Mine were <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ 1) FAX!!!!!!!!! and 2) no one important dies. Luckily, both of these happened.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Unfortunately, just because those two expectations were met doesn't mean the book actually made complete sense. It was a bit like that whole the-last-months-were-a-dream-wait-no-they-weren't-yes-they-were-never-mind-oh-and-by-the-way-max's-arm-works-again thing in the second or third book. If you don't look too closely, you can skim right over it and move on. As soon as you try to understand it, you're just like, "...What?" Which is sad, because it was the end. There will be no clarification. That was IT. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ One chapter really bothered me, which was the whole "I'm dead now but hopefully I contributed to the world and please save the environment and corporations are bad" monologue. And then she wasn't actually dead. I feel really bad saying this, because I wanted so, sooooooo badly for this book to be good, but the ending made zero sense.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Also, as a final note on Fax, I was glad that happened. But that scene at the end was just kind of creepy. I mean, they're what, fifteen? *shiver*  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Basically, it's good on a superficial level. As soon as you look too closely (or really try to understand anything at all), it's really disappointing. *sob* This book unfortunately did not deserve my fangirling (or begging my parents to take me to Target 15 minutes before it closed to get it).<br /><br />Would I recommend it? If you really like the characters, it at least ties up a few loose ends with them, but it also leaves a few questions. If you're looking for a super-amazing plot, than don't even THINK about reading it. I guess I would only recommend it if you need a sense of closure (series-wise, not necessarily character-wise).<br /><br />And, I nearly forgot. What was that garbage at the end with the "One girl's story ends, another is just beginning" thing? I was like, "I just finished a series that I've been waiting to finish since March... and YOU'RE ALREADY TRYING TO SELL ME ANOTHER BOOK?????" That was low. Really, that was pathetic. Absolutely terrible.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8162005834958200365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3251318120221024977">I. Am. PISSED!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! Now, I was patient for Febuary, but NOOOOOO James Patterson just HAD to move the release date to AUGUST!!!!!!!!!!!! *Deep Breath* Now, if they find Angel, I'll be happy. If Dylan leaves forever, I'll be happy. If Fax gets back together, I'll be happy. But I can't BE happy until this MOFO book comes out, now will I?!   <span id="freeText3251318120221024977" style="display:none">I. Am. PISSED!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! Now, I was patient for Febuary, but NOOOOOO James Patterson just HAD to move the release date to AUGUST!!!!!!!!!!!! *Deep Breath* Now, if they find Angel, I'll be happy. If Dylan leaves forever, I'll be happy. If Fax gets back together, I'll be happy. But I can't BE happy until this MOFO book comes out, now will I?! Ok, that's my rant! :P Oh, and the people that say that they're gonna burn every Max book if she and Dylan get together, here's a suggestion: Just burn every book that has Dylan in it! Or else, I'll have kill you. Nah, I'm just kiding! (Maybe)<br /><br /><b>Edit:</b><br /><br />. . . . I think I seriously just felt my heart crack. I'n not joking. This book was touching to me in a way that I felt like I was feeling everything that Max felt with Fang, Dylan, and everyone else, especially Angel. I just . . . I don't think it will be easy for me to forget about this book that <i>literaly</i> changed my whole point of view on books, but I don't think it will be hard for me to find another heroine to love like I've come to love Maximum Ride.<br /><br />Yeah, that last part was a total lie. I'm never going to find another character like I love Max, Fang, Nudge, Iggy, Gazzy, and Angel. Hell, even Dylan, Dr. Hans, Jeb, and Ari I've come to love! All because they're part of the Maximum Experience. It just . . . My heart will never feel the same without Max there, but I'll always have the stories . . . <br /><br />AND SOON THE MOVIE!</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PP/uVqd9p+8DxoC57TwBJejYcVbc+EIO5wZLuoeHSzEG2YeEHCNuh6TtNNgayQv6PoeWnhJ1zGm8eA0LSsS5qw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Jk6NAiNhmf4Z9tCZ5d6Ajne5QNC3pUnDh9KJNdjrVZgcaOTQmD9Qlr7dZPgSK4pRoeanGHkox6TcrM+EFainAg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2124120623751032802"><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official US Site</a><br/><a href='http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>Official UK Site</a><br/><a href='http://jimmypatterson.org' rel='nofollow noopener'>JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br/><a href='http://readkiddoread.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>ReadKiddoRead</a><br/><br/><br/><br/>James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books wo</span>
  <span id="freeText2124120623751032802" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Official US Site</a><br /><a href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Official UK Site</a><br /><a href="http://jimmypatterson.org" rel="nofollow noopener">JIMMY Patterson Books</a><br /><a href="http://readkiddoread.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadKiddoRead</a><br /><br /><br /><br />James Patterson is the world’s bestselling author and most trusted storyteller. He has created more enduring fictional characters than any other novelist writing today, with his Alex Cross, Michael Bennett, Women’s Murder Club, Private, NYPD Red, Daniel X, Maximum Ride, and Middle School series. He has sold over 380 million books worldwide and currently holds the Guinness World Record for the most #1 New York Times bestsellers. In addition to writing the thriller novels for which he is best known, among them The President Is Missing with President Bill Clinton, Patterson also writes fiction for young readers of all ages, including the Max Einstein series, produced in partnership with the Albert Einstein Estate. He is also the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on the New York Times adult and children’s bestseller lists.<br /> <br />The son of an insurance salesman and a schoolteacher, Patterson grew up in Newburgh, New York, and began casually writing at the age of nineteen. In 1969, he graduated from Manhattan College. He was given a full-ride scholarship to Vanderbilt University’s graduate program in English. He left Vanderbilt before getting his PhD due to complications involving the Vietnam War. <br /> <br />Instead, he moved to New York to become a junior copywriter for the advertising agency J. Walter Thompson, eventually becoming CEO of its North American company.<br /> <br />In 1976, while still working for J. Walter Thompson, Patterson published his first novel, The Thomas Berryman Number, with Little, Brown and Company. After being turned down by thirty-one publishers, it won the Edgar Award for Best First Novel. Patterson’s 1993 novel, Along Came a Spider, his first book to feature Alex Cross, was also his first New York Times bestseller in fiction.<br /> <br />In 2001, Morgan Freeman starred as Alex Cross in a film adaptation of Along Came a Spider, and Tyler Perry also played the character in the 2012 film Alex Cross. A film adaptation of Patterson’s middle-grade novel Middle School: The Worst Years of My Life was released in theaters in October 2016.<br /> <br />James Patterson has donated more than one million books to students, focusing on some of the most under-resourced schools and youth programs in the country. To date, he has donated $7.25 million to school and classroom libraries throughout the United States, and $2.1 million to independent bookstores and employees.<br /> <br />Patterson has recently donated over $35 million to his and his wife’s alma maters—the University of Wisconsin, Vanderbilt University, and Manhattan College—and he has established over four hundred Teacher and Writer Education Scholarships at twenty-one colleges and universities throughout the country. Patterson has also donated more than one million books to U.S. soldiers at home and overseas.<br /> <br />In May 2015, Patterson launched a children’s book imprint at Little, Brown—JIMMY Patterson—that is unwaveringly focused on one goal: turning kids into lifelong readers. This imprint also provides resources, strategies, and programs to serve teachers, parents, librarians, and booksellers. Patterson invests proceeds from the sales of JIMMY Patterson Books in pro-reading initiatives.<br /> <br />Patterson also founded ReadKiddoRead.com, a website designed to help parents, teachers, and librarians ignite a new generation’s excitement for reading. Awarded the National Book Foundation’s Innovations in Reading Prize and the American Library Association’s Great Websites for Kids, the site features thoughtful book reviews from a variety of genres and age ranges, a large and lively Facebook community, and contributions from other authors.<br /> <br />Patterson’s awards for adult and children’s literature include the Edgar Award, the International </span>
